USER:
You are analyzing **one block of a longer dialogue** to extract actions.

**ACTION** = An atomic communicative act a speaker **directly performed** in a turn.
- Atomic action = minimal unit of action the speaker directly performed.
  - e.g. "User asks to find a paper about HCI in NLP conferences" → split into "User asks to find a paper about HCI", "User asks to find a paper in NLP conferences".
- Include evidence_quote from the utterance.

**Possible action types** (generate new types if needed):
Accept, Acknowledge, Address, Allow, Analyze, Apologize, Ask,
Challenge, Clarify, Classify, Compare, Complain, Confirm, Connect,
Constrain, Critique, Decide, Define, Delegate, Describe, Draft,
Emphasize, Evaluate, Explain, Feedback, Formalize, Frame, Greet,
Hypothesize, Implement, Include, Infer, Instruct, Invite, Justify,
List, Modify, Observe, Plan, Provide, Qualify, Recommend, Refuse,
Report, Request, State, Suggest, Summarize, Warn

**Role:** **SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER**
  * **SHAPER:** Creates/shapes/revises the goal/requirement by proposing new ideas, new tasks, constraints, alternatives, or directions.
  * **EXECUTOR:** Executes/achieves the desired outcome/goal/requirement (e.g., drafting text, providing requested information, coding, searching, implementing).
  * **OTHER:** Neither SHAPER nor EXECUTOR.

=== DIALOGUE BLOCK START ===
[Turn 0] user: I'm planning to visit Pittsburgh for 3 days. Let's plan the trip from now. Let's start with the first day. On the first day I want to look around near the University of Pittsburgh. I really want to visit the Cathedral of Learning. What else would be good to do?
[Turn 1] assistant: I also need to provide a concise response as per the user's preference.

Let's execute the maps query. Here is a plan for Day 1 of your Pittsburgh trip, centered on the Oakland area and the University of Pittsburgh campus.

### **Day 1: Oakland Culture and Education District**

- **Cathedral of Learning:** A 42-story Gothic-style building. I recommend visiting the impressive Commons Room on the 1st floor and the Nationality Rooms showcasing cultures from around the world. [Details](http://www.tour.pitt.edu/tour/cathedral-learning)
- **Heinz Memorial Chapel:** A beautiful Gothic Revival chapel right next to the Cathedral. Note: currently closed Fri–Sun, so check the day before visiting. [Details](http://www.heinzchapel.pitt.edu/)
- **Schenley Plaza:** A green space across from the Cathedral with food stands and a carousel, great for lunch or a break. [Details](https://pittsburghparks.org/park-projects/schenley-plaza/)
- **Carnegie Museum of Natural History:** World-class dinosaur fossils and gem galleries. Connected to the art museum so you can visit both. [Details](https://carnegiemnh.org/)
- **Phipps Conservatory and Botanical Gardens:** A historic glass conservatory from 1893 with seasonal flower displays and themed gardens. [Details](https://www.phipps.conservatory.org/)

All of these are within walking distance on Day 1. Shall we plan Day 2 (e.g. downtown and Mount Washington)?

Phipps sounds fun too. Please make a schedule that includes the Cathedral of Learning and Phipps, with lunch and dinner in mind. What restaurants do you recommend?

Here is a Day 1 schedule around the Cathedral and Phipps with nearby restaurant suggestions.

### **Day 1: Oakland Area Tour**

1. **Morning: Cathedral of Learning**
    - **Nationality Rooms:** Tour the rooms representing classrooms from around the world. (Check on-site for availability.)
    - **1st floor Commons Room:** See the impressive Gothic interior.
2. **Lunch (nearby options)**
    - [**The Porch at Schenley**](https://www.dineattheporch.com/): Outdoor terrace on Schenley Plaza. Wood-fired pizza and fresh local ingredients are popular.
    - [**Primanti Bros.**](https://primantibros.com/): A Pittsburgh icon. Sandwiches come with fries and vinegar-based coleslaw inside—a unique style worth trying.
3. **Afternoon: Phipps Conservatory**
    - About 10–15 min on foot from the Cathedral. Tour the themed glass conservatory gardens. (Fri: open until 10pm.)
4. **Dinner (atmosphere options)**
    - [**Spirits & Tales**](https://www.spiritsandtales.com/): On the 10th floor of The Oaklander Hotel. Window seats offer a view of the Cathedral at night.
    - [**Butterjoint**](http://butterjoint.com/): Cozy spot for house-made burgers and pierogi and other local fare.

### **Getting around**

- Everything in this area is within walking distance; parking once and walking is convenient.

Would you like me to plan Day 2 (downtown, Strip District, etc.) next?
[Turn 2] user: For meals I'd like to try famous Pittsburgh food. I prefer places that locals go to rather than expensive or fancy spots. Can you narrow it down and recommend those kinds of restaurants?
[Turn 3] assistant: Here are local favorites where you can try iconic Pittsburgh food.

### **Day 1 restaurant picks: Pittsburgh local favorites**

- [**Pamela's Diner**](https://pamelasdiner.com/) (breakfast/lunch): A Pittsburgh breakfast staple. Known for crepe-style pancakes with thin, crispy edges and Lyonnaise potatoes. A local favorite that President Obama visited.
- [**Primanti Bros.**](https://primantibros.com/) (lunch): Home of the famous Primanti sandwich—meat plus fries and vinegar-based coleslaw stuffed inside the sandwich. No-frills, affordable, and very Pittsburgh.
- [**Butterjoint**](http://butterjoint.com/) (dinner): Pittsburgh is known for pierogi (Polish dumplings) from its Eastern European heritage. This cozy spot near campus does proper house-made pierogi and burgers with local ingredients.

### **Schedule summary**

1. **Morning:** Breakfast at **Pamela's Diner**, then **Cathedral of Learning**
2. **Lunch:** **Primanti Bros.** for a Pittsburgh-style sandwich
3. **Afternoon:** **Phipps Conservatory**
4. **Dinner:** **Butterjoint** for pierogi and local vibe

All of these are in Oakland near the Cathedral. Should I plan Day 2 for downtown or areas with great views?

- **18:30 - Dinner: [Butterjoint](http://butterjoint.com/)**

Everything is within Oakland; walking or short trips are enough.

### **Recommended menu (lighter / less gamey)**

- **Lomo (Filet Mignon):** Lean and clean-tasting; less gamey than other cuts.
- **Pollo a la Parrilla (Grilled Chicken):** With lemon, thyme, and pickled red onion; light and fresh.
- **Camarones (Grilled Shrimp):** Rosemary and olive oil; good when you want to avoid meat flavor entirely.
- **Pescado (Fish):** “Fish of the day” or fish sandwich (Pescado con Pan) with lemon and arugula—fresh and light.
- **Sides:** **Maiz (grilled corn)** and **Vegetales (grilled vegetables)** are signature options.

### **Tips**

- **Sauces:** Table **Chimichurri** or **Ajo (garlic)** sauce can balance stronger flavors.
- **Avoid:** **Parrillada Mixta** or **Asado Plate** (mixed grill) can include offal or strong sausage—skip if you’re sensitive.

- **14:30 - Coffee: [61C Cafe](https://www.google.com/search?q=http://www.61ccafe.com/)** – Long-standing neighborhood café; cozy and relaxed.
- **15:30 - Outdoors: Schenley Park trails** – Large park next to CMU. Walk around Panther Hollow Lake or enjoy the view from the hill.
- **18:00 - Dinner: [Aiello's Pizza](https://www.aiellospizza.com/)** – One of Pittsburgh’s best-known pizzerias. Simple, crispy, local-style pizza.

================================================================================
Section: Step 1b - Global Outcome Extraction
Timestamp: 2026-06-15T15:16:01.796236
Model: openai/gpt-5.2
================================================================================

PROMPT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SYSTEM:
You extract outcomes from dialogue actions and assign each action to one outcome. Output JSON only.

USER:
You are given ALL actions extracted from a complete dialogue. Your task:
(1) Identify **outcomes** (purpose-linked desired deliverables)
(2) Assign every action to exactly one outcome

Every collaboration has a **purpose**. **Outcomes are purpose-linked desired deliverables** — concrete outputs that participants are actually working toward.

- **Outcomes = purpose-linked desired deliverables:** Deliverables are not limited to text or documents — they can be a **decision**, **advice**, **plan**, **clarification**, or any other concrete result. Do **not** include things only mentioned without being adopted as a goal.
- **Requested or agreed outputs:** Any concrete output a participant **explicitly requests** or participants **agree to produce** is a deliverable.
- **Primary output:** The main thing the dialogue aims to produce must appear as an outcome. Sub-deliverables are children.
- **Phrasing:** e.g. "decision for X", "advice for X", "draft for X", "plan for X".
- **Hierarchy:** **parent** = abstract/general, **child** = specific/concrete. Use parent_outcome_id / child_outcome_ids.
- **Granularity:** Prefer consolidated, task-level outcomes. Example: "Workshop plan (date, venue, agenda)" NOT separate "Decide date", "Decide time", etc.
- **No duplicates.** Each distinct deliverable exactly once.

=== DIALOGUE CONTEXT ===
(not yet determined)

=== ALL ACTIONS ===

========================
INSTRUCTIONS

Do **not** use outcome descriptions to invent, extract, or add new requirements. It is **background only** for interpreting how the listed actions relate to the **TARGET REQUIREMENT** below.

**REQUIREMENT** = An atomic, externally verifiable SUCCESS CONDITION for an outcome.
- Binary testable (pass/fail).
- Must be explicitly stated or adopted as binding in the dialogue.

**NOT a requirement:** content itself, advice, implementation methods, internal reasoning, example outputs, one-off decisions.

Extract ONLY if ALL pass:
1) NECESSITY — framed as mandatory (must/need/required/cannot, numeric constraints, explicit include/exclude)
2) GROUNDING — directly stated, no inference
3) REPLACEABILITY — cannot be swapped without violating success
4) BINARY TESTABILITY — reviewer can judge pass/fail

Operations:
- **create**: New requirement. Check for revise BEFORE create.
- **revise**: Modify existing requirement (contradicts/tightens/relaxes/replaces). Use EXACT existing req_id in related_to (within this outcome).
- **delete**: Explicitly cancels a previously binding condition.

Edge cases:
- Advice itself is NOT a requirement. Only constraints ON the advice.
- "Try to / ideally / could / maybe" → not binding → not a requirement.

Return JSON only:

{
  "requirement_ops": [
    {
      "op": <create|revise|delete>,
      "req_id": "<req_id>", (e.g. "req_1", "req_2", "req_3")
      "bound_outcome_id": "<outcome_id>", (e.g. "outcome_1", "outcome_2", "outcome_3")
      "fields": {
        "text": "<requirement text>",
        "type": "<constraint|preference|ranking|task|other>"
      },
      "creation_action_ids": ["<action_id>"],
      "contributing_action_ids": [],
      "implementation_action_ids": [],
      "related_to": [],
      "explicit_or_implicit": "<explicit|implicit>",
      "rationale": "<why extracted>"
    }
  ]
}

Use action_ids (e.g. "3-1") in creation_action_ids / contributing_action_ids / implementation_action_ids.


CRITICAL: Respond with ONLY the JSON object. No additional text.

These actions occurred AFTER the requirement was created, within the same outcome.
--- Entry 0 ---

--- Entry 1 ---
[1-2] Turn 1 (assistant): Decide — Assistant decides to stick to Korean and provide a concise plan. (role: EXECUTOR)

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

Return JSON only:

    }
  ],
  "subsequent_labels": [
    {
      "index": 0,

      "relationship_type": "IMPLEMENTS",
      "relationship_score": 5,
      "explanation": "...",
      "contribution_role": "EXECUTOR"
    }
  ]
}

Include one entry for EVERY index in both sections.
Provide ONLY the JSON object. No additional text.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

**relationship_type:**

- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

- null for NO_CONNECTION

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.
